      "content after edit": [
        "After training is completed in this manner, when we perform inference during test time with this model, we first give the initial input as the first character at the first time step. Then, when the next character is predicted at that time step, we feed this character as the input for the next time step. In this way, inference is performed sequentially by taking the character predicted at each time step and using it as the input for the immediately following time step.\n\nHowever, the numbers shown here are from before the training was completed, as seen in the previous slide. If we perform inference with this pre-trained model as is, at the first time step, the prediction with the highest probability (character 'o') will come out as the prediction. This 'o' character will then be used as the input for the following time step, and this kind of sequential prediction will be performed.\n\nAs a reference, a model that feeds the prediction or output at the current time step as the input for the next time step during test time or inference is called an autoregressive model. Here, 'auto' does not mean automatic; rather, like the English word 'autography' meaning autobiography, it implies 'self' or 'by oneself.' And 'regressive' in autoregressive comes from regression, which is a model that performs some kind of prediction. In essence, the name autoregressive comes from the fact that the model uses its own output again as input to produce the next prediction."
      ]

      "content after edit": [
        "After training is completed in this manner, when we perform inference during test time with this model, we first give the initial input as the first character at the first time step. Then, when the next character is predicted at that time step, we feed this character as the input for the next time step. In this way, inference is performed sequentially by taking the character predicted at each time step and using it as the input for the immediately following time step.\n\nHowever, the numbers shown here are from before the training was completed, as seen in the previous slide. If we perform inference with this pre-trained model as is, at the first time step, the prediction with the highest probability (character 'o') will come out as the prediction. This 'o' character will then be used as the input for the following time step, and this kind of sequential prediction will be performed.\n\nAs a reference, a model that feeds the prediction or output at the current time step as the input for the next time step during test time or inference is called an autoregressive model. Here, 'auto' does not mean automatic; rather, like the English word 'autography' meaning autobiography, it implies 'self' or 'by oneself.' And 'regressive' in autoregressive comes from regression, which is a model that performs some kind of prediction. In essence, the name autoregressive comes from the fact that the model uses its own output again as input to produce the next prediction."
      ]
